## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology (population dynamics / growth models)
**Analysis**: The target is a time derivative dP_dt driven by current population size P (and possibly time t), which is the standard setup for continuous-time population growth models with density dependence, environmental forcing, and harvesting/mortality terms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited resources, constant per-capita rate)
- Time-trending intrinsic rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (gradual improvement/decline in environment affecting per-capita growth)
- Allometric/power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (nonlinear scaling of growth with population size)
- Logistic ODE (density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (crowding reduces growth; carrying capacity ~ 1/c1)
- Theta-logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible curvature of density dependence)
- Gompertz-type growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (per-capita growth declines ~ log(P), often for self-limiting growth)
- Allee effect (depensation): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (c2 * P - 1) (negative growth at low P due to mate limitation/cooperation)
- Constant-yield harvesting/mortality: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 (removal independent of P; can create extinction if c1 is large)
- Proportional harvesting/mortality: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (additional linear loss term shifts equilibria)
- Saturating harvest/predation (Holling-II style): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P / (P + c3) (removal saturates at high P)
- Seasonally forced growth: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * P * (1 - c3 * P) (periodic environment modulates intrinsic rate)
- Time-varying carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / (c1 + c2 * t)) (resource base changes with time)
- Environmental deterioration/improvement factor: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * exp(c2 * t) (exponentially changing habitat quality affecting growth)
- Immigration/emigration offset: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) + c2 (constant net influx/outflux added to endogenous dynamics)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope тЖТ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects тЖТ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay тЖТ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior тЖТ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects тЖТ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Per-capita growth structure: (dP_dt) / P depending only on P suggests density-dependent regulation (e.g., linear in P implies logistic-like regulation).
- Carrying capacity signature: a negative quadratic term in P (e.g., -c * P**2) implies a stable equilibrium near P тЙИ 1/c (after factoring).
- Depensation/Allee signature: an extra factor like (c0 * P - 1) or (P - c0) implies negative growth below a threshold and bistability (extinction vs persistence).
- Gompertz signature: a log(c0 / P) term implies diminishing per-capita growth roughly proportional to log-size, often fitting growth that slows earlier than logistic.
- Harvesting signature: subtracting c0 (constant removal) or c0 * P (proportional removal) lowers equilibria and can introduce extinction thresholds.
- Saturating loss signature: loss terms like P / (P + c0) indicate bounded predation/harvest capacity, typically reducing pressure at low P and capping removal at high P.
- Seasonal/environmental forcing: sin(c * t) (or similar periodic t-dependence) in the growth coefficient indicates cyclic resource or climate drivers.
- Nonstationary habitat capacity: denominators like (c0 + c1 * t) inside 1 - P/(...) indicate time-varying carrying capacity, causing drifting equilibria over time.

Key structural facts:
- **No \(t\)-dependence** at all.
- It is the sum of **(i)** a **cubic polynomial in \(P\)** (because \(P\cdot(\text{linear})\cdot(\text{linear})\)) and **(ii)** a **\(P^{1/3}\)** term.
- No logs, no exponentials, no sines, no rational \(1/(aP+b)\) terms.

So any matching candidate must be able (by parameter choice) to become exactly тАЬcubic polynomial in \(P\) + constant┬╖\(P^{1/3}\)тАЭ, and must eliminate any \(t\)-terms and any non-polynomial-in-\(P\) functions (log/exp/sin/rational), unless they can be set to zero.

### 1
Has logs in \(P\), log in \(t\), and exp in \(P\), plus constant term. Can zero out log/exp coefficients, but then becomes \(c0 P^{1/3}+c1\). Cannot produce the required cubic polynomial term. **No.**

GT: c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*P**c6
Candidates evaluated: 67
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) and compare each candidate to it.

## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT is:
$$f(P) = 0.7689 \cdot (-1 + P/8.670) \cdot (1 - P/14.333) \cdot P + 0.7689 \cdot P^{1/3}$$

Let me expand the polynomial part:
$$(-1 + P/8.670)(1 - P/14.333) = -1 + P/14.333 + P/8.670 - P^2/(8.670 \times 14.333)$$
$$= -1 + P(1/14.333 + 1/8.670) - P^2/124.268$$

Computing: $1/14.333 + 1/8.670 = 0.06977 + 0.11534 = 0.18511$

So: $(-1 + P/8.670)(1 - P/14.333) \cdot P = -P + 0.18511P^2 - P^3/124.268$

Multiplied by 0.7689:
$$= -0.7689P + 0.14233P^2 - 0.006190P^3$$

Plus $0.7689 P^{1/3}$

So GT = $-0.006190 P^3 + 0.14233 P^2 - 0.7689 P + 0.7689 P^{1/3}$

**Key features of GT:**
- It's a function of P only (no t dependence)
- Contains basis functions: $P^3$, $P^2$, $P$, $P^{1/3}$
- It's a cubic polynomial in P plus a $P^{1/3}$ term

Now I'll check each candidate. For candidates with `t` dependence, I need to verify if the `t` terms can be zeroed out. For candidates without the right basis functions, they cannot match.

**Required basis:** $P^{1/3}$ (or equivalent fractional power), $P$, $P^2$, $P^3$

Let me systematically go through candidates, focusing on which ones have the right structure.

### Candidates with `t` dependence that CAN be zeroed:
- Candidates 1, 6, 8, 12, 18, 19, 27, 28, 29, 30, 37, 46, 47, 49, 51, 52, 57, 61, 64, 65, 67: These have `t` terms. If the `t` coefficients can be set to 0, the remaining terms must match GT.

### Candidates with wrong basis functions (no possible match):

**Candidates needing $P^{1/3}$ AND cubic polynomial:**

The GT is: $aP^3 + bP^2 + cP + dP^{1/3}$

Let me check candidates that could potentially represent this:

**Candidate 11:** $P^{c0} \cdot c1 + P^{c2} \cdot c3 + c4 + c5 \cdot \exp(P \cdot c6)$

This has two power-law terms plus a constant plus an exponential. Setting $c5=0$ (to kill exp), we get $c1 P^{c0} + c3 P^{c2} + c4$. This gives only two power-law terms plus a constant - we need four terms ($P^3, P^2, P, P^{1/3}$). **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 2:** $c0 P^2 + c1 P + c2 P/(P+c3) + c4 P/(c5 P + c6) + c7/(c5 P + c6)$

This is a rational function. Let me see if it can produce $P^3 + P^2 + P + P^{1/3}$. Rational functions cannot produce $P^{1/3}$. **NO MATCH.**

Let me focus on candidates that have $P^{1/3}$ (or $P^{c}$ with free exponent) AND enough polynomial terms.

**Candidates with $P^{1/3}$:** 1, 3, 5, 8, 16, 18, 21, 25, 29, 38, 44, 61

**Candidates with $P^{c}$ (free exponent):** 11, 25, 30, 31, 32, 33, 39, 58, 59

**Candidates with $\sqrt{P}$:** 17, 36, 42, 43, 45, 53, 57, 67

$\sqrt{P} \neq P^{1/3}$, so $\sqrt{P}$ candidates need another mechanism. **All $\sqrt{P}$ candidates: NO MATCH** (unless they also have a free exponent).

**Candidate 59:** $\sqrt{P} \cdot c0 + P^{c1} \cdot c2 + c3 + c4 \exp(Pc5) + c6 \exp(Pc7)$
Set $c0=0$, $c4=0$, $c6=0$: leaves $c2 P^{c1} + c3$. Only one power term. **NO MATCH.**

Let me now carefully check the most promising candidates.

### Candidate 21: $c0 P^{1/3} + c1 P^2 + c2 P + c3 \sin(c4 P + c5) + c6$
